Education News

Chairman Chiang Orders Provinces and Cities to Promote Literacy Education, with Labor Service as the Center of School and Public Education to Change the Previous Lazy, Scattered, Selfish Bad Habits

(Hankou Correspondence) Chairman Chiang issued an order on the 1st to all provinces and cities to promote literacy education, so that students and citizens alike can recognize labor as their duty, service as their vocation, and prepare for universal compulsory labor. The original order stated: "National rejuvenation, education is the most important task. In addition to the predetermined political work this year, all provinces should pay special attention to education. Provincial chairmen and education commissioners must do their best to implement the promotion and popularization methods. If adults can teach children to read, those with knowledge can teach those with less knowledge, all with a spirit of duty and mutual assistance, to improve people's intelligence and morality, and continue to work hard, the effect of a month will surely be achieved. In particular, in addition to training citizens and improving their spirit and life according to the requirements of the New Life Movement, such as neatness, cleanliness, simplicity, frugality, speed, and certainty, labor and service must be the center of school education and public education, so that students and citizens alike can recognize labor as their duty, service as their vocation, change the previous lazy, scattered, selfish bad habits, and strive to be healthy citizens. In this way, with educational methods, publicizing the spirit, the people will be able to persuade each other to work and happily serve the country and society, which is also a preparation for universal compulsory labor. In addition to separate orders, I hope you will earnestly follow and implement it." (2nd)

After the Loss of Rare Books from the Changshu Library, Qian Xijin Has Returned a Portion

(Changshu Correspondence) The ancient books treasured by this county's library are extremely rich and valuable, surpassing those of other places. Recently, the current curator, Xiao Diyi, discovered that many ancient books were missing from the library. He reported the situation to the Education Bureau. After detailed investigation, it was determined that the losses occurred when Qian Xijin was the previous curator. Qian did not complete the transfer procedures, and there is a suspicion of embezzlement. Qian has now been reassigned as the curator of the Heyang Agricultural Education Center. The Bureau ordered him to come to the city. The county government, considering that this case is related to local culture, first ordered the Education Bureau to detain Qian. A telegram has been sent to the province requesting legal action. The stolen books amount to hundreds of volumes, all treasured manuscripts and ancient editions of exceptional rarity. It is anticipated that all the books in the library will be examined and then investigated thoroughly.

The Problem of Chinese Children's Education

— Wang Shijie

Broadcasted yesterday on Children's Day at the Central Broadcasting Station

Today is Children's Day. All our fathers, mothers, brothers, and sisters throughout the country should bless the children of the entire nation and, at the same time, speak out for their rights.

We know that the so-called "Rights of Man" (simply put, "Human Rights") had already been recognized by the laws of France and America by the end of the 18th century, the time of the French and American Revolutions, because they incorporated the so-called "Declaration of the Rights of Man and of the Citizen" or the "Bill of Rights" into their revolutionary constitutions. By the end of the 19th century, many other countries had also accepted the theories of the French and American revolutionary eras in their constitutions or other legal codes. However, by and large, the efforts of civilized humanity during the 18th and 19th centuries focused on the rights and welfare of adults. Even in civilized nations, the rights that children should enjoy in the family and in society had not yet received adequate attention.

However, Rousseau, the great French thinker who most strongly advocated human rights theories in the 18th century, did not speak solely for adults. In his "Social Contract," Rousseau had already argued for the rights of all mankind. In his famous work "Emile," he argued even more specifically for the rights of children. He was not only a political thinker but also an educator. His basic views were: first, most of a person's life is determined during childhood; most of a person's happiness is created or destroyed during childhood. Second, children's education should be scientific. His "Social Contract" is known as the draft of the "Declaration of the Rights of Man," and his "Emile" is also known as the "Declaration of the Rights of Children."

In recent times, Rousseau's theories have gradually gained public recognition, and the importance of children's issues has become universally acknowledged. We often hear people say, "The 20th century should be a century for children." Now that a third of the 20th century has passed, we can see what achievements modern progressive countries have made in their efforts to promote child welfare and use them as a reference.

Children's Education

In general, in modern countries, the period of compulsory education for children is roughly from the ages of six or seven to fourteen. Some countries have recently extended the age of compulsory education to secondary school age, i.e., sixteen years old (e.g., England) or even eighteen years old (e.g., France and some American states). This is a kind of progress that people in the 18th and 19th centuries could not have dreamed of. This is one.

Children's Health

In order to protect children's health, in recent years - especially in the last one or two decades - many countries have established many new systems and adopted many new methods, such as special protection for pregnant women and mothers, compulsory prevention of diseases such as smallpox and diphtheria, control of milk and other children's foods, strict school health inspections, and promotion of children's health knowledge. The result has been a sharp decrease in infant mortality rates in various countries. For example, in England, the infant mortality rate has been reduced by half in the short span of the last three or four decades (in 1883, the mortality rate per thousand children was 146; in 1927, it was 70). This is two.

Relief for Orphaned and Destitute Children

In many countries, orphaned and destitute children used to rely almost entirely on private charitable organizations for relief. Now, this has gradually changed to state relief. Germany after the European War is the most obvious example. The legal status of illegitimate children has also greatly improved in recent years, or even become completely equal to that of legitimate children. Russia is an obvious example. This is also a revolution in traditional legal concepts. This is three.

Protection of Child Labor

In the early stages of the Industrial Revolution in Europe, children were the biggest victims. For example, the conditions of child laborers in British textile factories in the early 19th century and in Chinese silk and yarn factories today are so miserable that people simply cannot imagine them without experiencing them firsthand. Now, in general, countries have prohibited children under the age of fourteen from working in factories. The International Labor Conference has also incorporated this restriction into international conventions. Young people from the age of fourteen to around twenty-one are also subject to various protections under the labor laws of various countries. This is four.

Children's Crime

In general, progressive countries have adopted the following two policies in recent years regarding children's crime: first, raising the age of criminal responsibility. In the past, even very young children could be regarded as criminals and held criminally liable. For example, Roman law recognized that children over the age of seven could become criminals. Now, many countries' criminal laws still consider children under the age of seventeen or eighteen to be only partially criminally responsible. Second, the establishment of juvenile courts. Now, many countries use only education and not punishment to correct delinquent children, and only special juvenile courts are used to try them, not ordinary courts. This is five.

The above are only a few of the most salient points, but even these few points can give a glimpse of the achievements of modern countries in their efforts to address children's issues. Today, when we speak out for the children of the entire nation, all of the above issues should naturally be taken into consideration. However, since my role is in the field of education, I would like to say a few more words about the education of Chinese children.

I have previously spoken on this radio station that in the past twenty years or so of the Republic of China, in terms of the number of students, our higher education has expanded a hundredfold, secondary education has expanded eightfold, but primary education has only expanded fourfold. In the first year of the Republic of China, the number of primary school students was over 2.7 million; in the twentieth year of the Republic of China, it was still only over 11 million. These figures show that our education has not been fully extended to children in the primary school stage.

Recently, public opinion in the country has gradually focused on the elimination of illiteracy, which is indeed an important task, because the existence of a large number of illiterate people can make it difficult to promote all material construction work and to implement all spiritual construction work (such as instilling national consciousness and completing civic training). However, in order to eliminate illiteracy, on the one hand, all young people or adults who have passed the age of primary school should receive a minimal amount of supplementary education. On the other hand, all school-age children must receive a minimal amount of compulsory education. Compared to the two, the latter is more important than the former, because if compulsory primary education cannot be popularized, the source of illiteracy cannot be cut off. Even if current illiterate people can receive some kind of supplementary education, illiterate people will still continue to emerge. Therefore, our future efforts must especially focus on the compulsory education of school-age children. The population of our country is commonly estimated to be 400 million. School-age children (assumed to be six to twelve years old) are commonly estimated to account for one-tenth of the total population, i.e., 40 million people. As mentioned earlier, the number of school-age children currently in school is approximately 12 million. The number of school-age children who have not been able to enroll in school is approximately 28 million. How can we ensure that these 28 million or more school-age children all receive a minimal amount of compulsory education? This is our current serious problem.

In order to answer this question, we must first decide on the minimum length of compulsory education. Recently, the government's assumption and the public's advocacy seem to recognize that the period of compulsory education should be set at four years. However, a four-year compulsory education system cannot be achieved in one step. Therefore, the government plans to gradually increase the length of compulsory education from one year to four years. The implementation of compulsory education can therefore be divided into several phases. The period from 1935 to 1939 can be set as the first phase. During these five years, various places can gradually implement compulsory education for school-age children, and the duration of compulsory education can be temporarily set at one year, ensuring that by the end of 1939, one year of compulsory education has been popularized in all provinces and cities across the country. Next, the period from 1940 to 1944 will be designated as the second phase. At that time, the period of compulsory education for school-age children can be changed to two years. During these five years, two years of compulsory education must be gradually popularized in various provinces and cities. Further, compulsory education may be directly changed to four years to achieve the expected standard.

As for the teacher problem, on the one hand, we must add primary school teacher training institutions for the purpose of adding primary schools. But if we also (1) strictly implement the system of industry-department compilation, (2) fully implement the number of students in existing schools, and (3) improve private schools, there are still many existing teachers and school buildings that can be utilized. If we also adopt (4) the itinerant teaching system (i.e., setting up itinerant teachers) and (5) the teaching assistant system, the need for new teachers can also be greatly reduced. What is most difficult may still be the funding problem. However, if each child receives one year of compulsory education, if it is handled properly, the national expenditure should be no more than five yuan. If so, then making the current 28 million out-of-school school-age children receive one year of compulsory education will cost no more than 140 million yuan. If, as mentioned earlier, five years are used as the period for popularizing one year of compulsory education, the annual amount required is less than 30 million yuan. If this fee is further shared by the local and central governments - if the local government bears two-thirds and the central government subsidizes one-third - then even if both central and local finances are difficult, there should be a way to set it up. If we look at the central government's finances, the total expenditure for this year is approximately 800 million yuan, and the expenditure on central education is only about 3%. If another one-eightieth (10 million yuan) of the total expenditure is transferred to be used for the above-mentioned

the work of compulsory education can definitely be done. In short, the popularization of compulsory primary education is a very serious issue. On the one hand, we must not take it lightly, underestimate the complexity and difficulty of this problem. At the same time, we must not see it as too difficult, and especially must not be too afraid of difficulties. Our central and local governments, especially those in the country who are engaged in education, should, from now on, make up their minds, persevere, and promote and complete this great work of national rejuvenation, ensuring that the term "compulsory education" immediately breaks away from the stage of propaganda and enters the stage of implementation. As long as we have the determination and work hard, the recent examples of the Soviet Union and Poland can give us great encouragement, because these countries were in a situation similar to ours a few years ago in terms of the number of illiterate people.

The government has recently announced that the academic year of 1935 (August 1935 to July 1936) is China's Children's Year. We earnestly hope that everyone will work together to make our Children's Year the year in which compulsory primary education in China truly begins to be implemented.

Ministry of Education Medical Education Committee Resolution

(Nanjing, 4th) The Medical Education Committee of the Ministry of Education held a meeting at the Ministry on the 4th, both in the morning and afternoon. More than ten people, including Pang Jingzhou and Jin Baoshan, attended. Yan Fuqing chaired the meeting. Minister of Education Wang Shijie reported on the significance of the meeting, and Jin Shanzhen reported on the process of revising and organizing the curriculum standards and equipment standards. The following resolutions were made: (1) The outline of the medical school curriculum was revised and approved. (2) The outline of the curriculum for medical specialty schools was approved. (3) The time allocation table for each academic year of the curriculum outline for medical schools and medical specialties was assigned to Zhao Shiqing, Zhu Zhanggeng, Huang Jianzhong, Hu Ding'an, Wu Xiangfeng, Zhu Heng, and Duan Zuo for formal organization, to be submitted to the Ministry for review. (4) Explanations and teaching material outlines from various fields will be submitted to the Ministry for distribution to various medical schools for reference and research, and concrete opinions will be submitted within one year for revision. (5) The draft equipment standards for medical schools and medical specialties were revised and approved. (6) The Midwifery Education Committee and the Nursing Education Committee will be merged into this committee, and two specialized committees will be established, called the Midwifery Education Specialized Committee and the Nursing Education Specialized Committee.

Sports News

China Wins International Volleyball Championship; Defeats Russia 41 to 25 in Last Night's Finals; Qiu Guangxie's Spiking like Cannonballs Stuns the Audience

The international volleyball tournament (international style) organized by the YMCA included teams from China, Russia, the United States, and the Jewish community, playing in a single round-robin format. The Chinese and Russian teams had successively defeated the United States and the Jewish community. Last night's final match at 7:30 PM drew a full house, marking the YMCA volleyball tournament's first grand occasion. The Chinese and Russian teams were strong, making for a very intense competition. After losing the first set, the Chinese team was fortunate to have effective teamwork and defense. Qiu Guangxie's fierce spiking helped them win two consecutive sets, reversing the defeat with a score of two to one and winning the championship. In the other match, the United States defeated the Jewish community. The results are as follows:

China 52—14 Eleven to Fifteen Fifteen to Three Fifteen to Seven Russia

United States 28—41 Eleven to Fifteen Fifteen to Two Fifteen to Eleven Jewish

First Set

After the China-Russia match began, the atmosphere in the hall suddenly became tense. Russia displayed fierce momentum, scoring two consecutive points. China responded in kind, scoring four points. Soon after, the Russian team added two more points, and China immediately evened the score at six to six. The back-and-forth play was extremely balanced. Russian team captain Bulo Gufei's spiking was exceptionally fierce, while Chinese player Qiu Guangxie's spikes were like thunder, impossible to defend against. Coupled with Chen Zongqi's skillful setting, the combination was seamless. They once took the lead with a score of ten to seven. Unexpectedly, their formation became disorganized later on, and the Russian team seized the opportunity, winning the first set with a score of fifteen to eleven.

[Photo caption] The Chinese Championship Team of the Shanghai International Volleyball Tournament (from right to left, back row): Li Yaohua, Tan Lijian, Coach Chen Bingde, Zheng Yiquan, Mai Bingyao; (front row) Chen Zongqi, Captain Qiu Gengxie, Wei Dingyi, Zhou Dayun (Huifang Photo)

Second Set

After suffering a minor setback, the Chinese team rallied and strengthened its morale. With Qiu Guangxie, Chen Zongqi, and Wei Dingyi in the front, Chen set the ball in the middle, and Qiu and Wei launched attacks from the left and right. The heavy, cannonball-like spikes made it impossible for the opponent to defend, earning continuous cheers from the audience. With stable ball retrieval, the Chinese team scored eight consecutive points. The Russian team was flustered and at a loss. The Chinese team's momentum grew stronger, and when they reached fifteen points, the Russian team had only scored three.

Third Set

After each team won a set, the competition in the third set became even more intense. At this critical juncture, with the championship on the line, China scored two consecutive points. Since both losing and serving the ball do not award points, they were cautious and strived for the right to serve. Russia managed to add two points. Afterward, China took the lead with a score of six to two. After Russia earned the serve and added two points, the serve returned to China. Russian player Bulo Gufei tried hard to spike, but all of his attempts were cleverly blocked by Chinese players Qiu Guangxie and Chen Zongqi. Qiu Guangxie used his ape-like arm to spike and scored four consecutive points. The Russian team called a timeout to boost their morale, but it was to no avail. After twelve to four, the teams held on for a long time, with neither side willing to give up. Although the Russian team managed to gain three points, they were ultimately defeated by China with a score of fifteen to seven, and China won the championship. The lineups were as follows:

China: Chen Zongqi, Qiu Guangxie, Wei Dingyi, Zheng Yiquan, Zhou Dayun, Mai Bingyao

Russia: Bulo Gufei, Ge Liemafu, Xu Luohuo Fufujiluote Jingge, Sha Lin, Xu Situohuo Fu

After the match, YMCA Sports Department Chairman McKenno presented the awards. The Navy YMCA won the Group A championship, the Russian Overseas Chinese won the Group B championship, and China won the international championship. Each team received a silver cup, and the audience dispersed amidst cheers.

Commercial News

Finance: Gold Price Fluctuates Throughout the Day—Result: No Change—

Yesterday, the gold market was calm. The central bank continued to sell wheat, and the exchange rate rose again after gathering momentum, but the upward trend was blocked, and it once fell below the 70 yuan mark. However, sellers were not strong, and the short positions were slightly covered when the price was low. In the end, the market was extremely calm. According to foreign news, China will consult with Britain, France, Belgium, the United States, Japan, and other countries on reforming the currency system and international loans. The off-market trading opened and immediately rose to 75.6 yuan. The central bank's official exchange rate was announced, with British pounds rising slightly and American dollars remaining unchanged. The customs gold unit rose by 1.9 percent, and the standard gold price rose again to 909 yuan and 70 cents, starting a high market. After the opening, it continued to rise, but because banks took advantage of the high price to sell, Chinese merchants lacked a large appetite to buy. The exchange rate became strong. It was anticipated that HSBC's official exchange rate would rise by 125 for British pounds and 3125 for American dollars, and the price gradually fell back. The central bank sold again, and the domestic market became looser, once falling below the 70 yuan mark. However, because banks took advantage of the low price to buy in and large investors also maintained the price, it was pulled up immediately. There was quite a lot of fluctuation in the middle. Later, Chinese merchants covered their short positions, and the market tightened slightly after the exchange rate became strong, forming an upward trend. However, due to the high pressure of banks selling at high prices and the central bank's sales appetite, the price gradually fell again. However, the market was still calm, and after falling, it turned to fluctuation. At noon, the situation seemed stable, and the afternoon market opened calmly. Small investors saw that the rising trend had stopped again and tended to sell, and large investors took the opportunity to supply, stabilizing and then weakening, and once falling slightly. The first telegram from the Indian silver market reported no change, which allowed the market to maintain its stability and gradually recover. However, the market was sluggish and lacked change. Although the second report from the Indian silver market showed an increase of 1.1.1 anna, at this time, the price fluctuated around 4 yuan. Finally, large investors came to buy in slightly, and floating shorts also bought, and the market closed stably. The day's market was calm, and the overall trend fluctuated. If there were no exchange rate pressure, the trend seemed to have a rebound. The day's market situation is recorded below:

The morning opening was 876 yuan and 30 cents, an increase of 1 yuan and 50 cents from the previous close. Wanxing, Huixiang, Yuanmao Yong, and others were buying in, rising to 7 yuan and 80 cents. Huabi released June US dollars at 375, and Fuxing, Yongfu Yu, Dadecheng, Yonglichang, Dadelihuixiang Yuehu were reduced to 3 yuan. Yicheng Wanxing Tongtaichang took advantage of the low price to cover their shorts, rising to 4 yuan. It was anticipated that HSBC's official exchange rate would rise by 125 for British pounds and 3125 for American dollars. Fuxing Yong Huixiang Hengyu Yingxiang Yiyu Fuyu Qingfa Yongshen Dayong and others sold together, falling to within 05 cents. At this time, because Hengyu Dadecheng and others were still buying in, it rose to 2 yuan and 30 cents. The central bank released May US dollars at 625, and Huixiang Dadecheng Hengyu Yingxiang sold their positions one after another, breaking through the 70 yuan mark and falling to 69 yuan and 80 cents. Zhengjin bought current US dollars at 9375, Magali bought June US dollars at 625, and Hengyu Fuxing Yong Dadecheng Yuanmao Yong Yuanchang Yong Yongli took advantage of the low price to cover their shorts, gradually rising to 73 yuan and 90 cents. Since the silver dollar market entered a normal state last month, it has gradually become stable recently. The previous atmosphere of infighting has been completely swept away. Yesterday, the interbank loan rate in the market remained at 9% for both the morning and afternoon sessions. The '劃頭' [margin call rate] also remained unchanged, with no additional premiums added. In terms of interbank loan transactions, over 3.9 million yuan were transferred in the morning session, with over 400,000 yuan in new transactions. Coinage of 2.94 Million Yuan in March

Coinage situation of the Central Mint in March: The review committee of the said mint announced that after reviewing 1.9 million yuan in new coins of the 23rd year sent by the Central Mint for review in March of the 24th year, the committee appointed metallurgist Ge Laide to conduct random inspections in accordance with the regulations. The fineness and weight were found to be in compliance with the silver standard coin minting regulations. A total of 588 certificates were issued, numbered from (23)12264 to (23)12851. In addition, 124 Class B factory bars (880 fineness) minted by the Central Mint in March of the 24th year, numbered from 52617 to 52740, were also monitored during the calibration marking by the committee, which appointed metallurgist Ge Laide to supervise the process in accordance with regulations. The fineness and weight were listed and registered. In addition to approving their separate release, this announcement is hereby issued for general knowledge.

U.S. New Cotton Rises Strongly Old Cotton Also Stabilizes

Yesterday, the U.S. cotton market opened weak and inactive. Because brokers closed their long positions and foreign firms sold, and the market deeply believed that a certain merchant bought foreign cotton and sold off U.S. cotton to hedge, prices for all months fell slightly from 3 to 10 [unclear unit]. At noon, it was heard that Secretary of Agriculture Wallace stated at a press conference that the cotton processing tax would not increase before August 1. At the same time, reports from Wall Street indicated that the government would soon have effective methods for new cotton. As a result, new cotton rose, and old cotton was able to stabilize. It is said that Liverpool firms are very interested in buying because the difference between new and old cotton is very large. Peers and New Orleans also bought, and shorts covered their positions. There were not many sellers. Holders intend to wait for the development of government policies. The subsequent market price reversed, especially in the near months. At closing, old cotton fell 4 [unclear unit], new cotton rose 10 to 15 [unclear unit], spot prices fell 5 [unclear unit], British cotton spot prices fell 4 points, and futures fell 12 points. Indian cotton rose due to good current demand, short covering, and speculative buying. 平果爾 Ping Guo Er rose 1.25 rupees, 奥姆辣 Aomula rose 1.5 rupees, and 白羅溪 Bai Luoxi rose 3.25 rupees. Silk and Tea - Chinese and Japanese Silk Merchants Have Vastly Different Mentalities - Non-Selling Unless Satisfied Price vs. Simply Seeking to Sell and Profit -

The transaction volume in the local foreign firm silk market is sparse. The main reason is that domestic silk merchants insist on not selling unless they have a satisfactory price. They disregard overseas market trends and still have the same bad mentality as in the past. Japanese silk has gradually shown signs of offering long-滞 [lagging, stale] goods onto the market due to insufficient supply. Therefore, the Yokohama market price is often around 580 yen. They are unwilling to let it rise and also unwilling to let it fall. They are willing to accept even a slightly lower price. This is a key business tip in recent years.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Shen Shou Ruo)

The more contentment there is in the hearts of all human beings, the less the danger of destruction. Do not believe that the insatiable greed of aggressors poses a danger of being defeated and destroyed by a general assault; the insatiable greed of speculators poses a danger of ruining their reputations and even leading to suicide… The only thing that one can be insatiable about without danger, but rather makes your life secure, is the continuous, in-depth study of knowledge and skills.

It is easy to awaken someone who is simply having a delusional dream; but if they have that dream and also start having complex dreams within dreams, then it is not easy to awaken them! For example, dreaming of getting rich out of thin air is a very simple dream. If you can't get rich, it's easy to wake up. But if, while having a dream of getting rich, you then have a dream within a dream about how you will build a Western-style house, buy a car, and take a concubine after you get rich, then it is difficult to awaken them from their delusion!

Viewing Things This Way

— Wang Jingyuan

Casually strolling down the street, or wandering in the sea of people, quietly observing the myriad forms of the common folk is actually more meaningful than visiting a zoo.

In terms of character: some are brave as lions, some are timid as mice, some are greedy as wolves, some are docile as sheep, some are cunning as foxes, some are treacherous as foxes, some are venomous as snakes and scorpions, some are foolish as deer and pigs, some are × as ××... People of all sorts can be symbolized by various animals, and then a phenomenon of various animals active will immediately appear in the mind: some pursue sexual desire, some fight for food; their purpose is nothing more than to solve the problems of food and sex that their nature requires, which is no different from other animals. How can it be called a sin? Only their skills have really surpassed other animals: such as kidnapping, scams, prostitution, body-in-a-box, what adulterous woman kills her husband, what murder for money, etc., none of which can be done by other animals. Is it not more meaningful to watch higher animals actively seeking food and sex than to visit a zoo where animals enjoy food and sex while sitting idly by, their nature submerged?

Humans originally evolved from animals. Being too serious only creates troubles. Viewing things this way, one can be at ease!

Take the author's life as an example: to view it as "sitting on the cold bench" is boring; but if one regards oneself as the "Monkey King," sitting facing south, issuing orders, and jumping around with the little monkeys, it is just like the realm of the Monkey King of Huaguo Mountain in the Journey to the West, is it not delightful! Is it not delightful!

Also, one evening on Penglai Road, I saw a group of men walking around a woman. I thought: if we were to implement Zhang Jingsheng's advocated beautiful nude parade, taking off our clothes completely, under the moonlight, it would be ten thousand times more beautiful than a group of dogs wearing a fur coat chasing a female dog.

Wang the Blind

— Bo Guang

In our town, no one doesn't know the great name of Wang the Blind. In fact, Wang the Blind is a begging vagrant. Why is it worth remembering him? But this beggar's reputation is too great. Not only does everyone in this town know him, but also people within a radius of dozens of miles know his character.

He begs in the market every first and fifteenth of the month. He must beg a copper coin from each business or household he passes before he will leave. At first, it was very difficult, but after a long time, each family saw him without even stepping onto the stairs and already had a copper coin pinched in their hands waiting for him.

But he is very frugal, saving up the copper coins he begs, and has actually accumulated thousands of yuan. Many small businessmen borrow money from him, and he charges an interest of two and a half cents. In this way, his money is rolling in more and more.

In recent years, he has taken in many "adopted sons." Children from wealthy families are very pampered, while beggars are considered very lowly. The idea is that giving children to beggars to be their sons makes it easy for them to grow up. Every year on the Dragon Boat Festival, he buys many fans and handkerchiefs to give to his adopted sons. People who receive his gifts have to give him one or two silver dollars. So, when he encounters holidays, he always eats his fill of wine and meat. Such a beggar can be praised as a "strange beggar."

The day before yesterday was his sixtieth birthday. Besides many disciples, grandsons, and little beggars, many "parents-in-law" and adopted sons came. He was so anxious that he had no choice but to go to the tavern to book more than a dozen tables of banquets, making a big ruckus. Such a beggar can be praised as a "strange beggar."

Pregnancy

— Huang Baiying

Pregnancy, this matter, on the journey of women's lives, who can avoid it? Only those women whose physiology has become abnormal.

When a woman is pregnant, men always feel it contains infinite mystery. Especially those beautiful young girls, newly married not long ago, suddenly swaying their high bulging bellies as they walk out the door, become the focus of attention for many men who specialize in gossiping about women. In the expressions of their eyebrows and eyes, there seems to be a common exclamation mark of surprise: "How can her belly be so high so quickly!"

Originally, pregnancy is an inevitable phenomenon after men and women are combined, and there is nothing extraordinary about it. However, the reason why women consider it shameful is because of the issue of physical beauty. This is different from the shyness women feel about marriage.

If a woman has already gone through two or one childbirth, pregnancy becomes a very ordinary matter.

A woman who is in the early stages of pregnancy feels uneasy in her daily life, and is also very uneasy in her spirit, because she instinctively anticipates the extreme pain of childbirth.

In the end, is pregnancy a joyful thing or a sad thing?

From my feelings, pregnancy is indeed a sad thing. -- Capitalists who generally hope for sons to carry on the family line are of course an exception. -- If a young couple's wife becomes pregnant, it is certainly unpleasant for the wife, and even more distressing for the husband. Young people are in the golden age of enjoying love. If there is a son in the middle, then the love between men and women often changes, even breaks down. Moreover, with a son, a sum of money for infant expenses must be added to the already unmanageable living expenses!

Many opinions are consistent: young people should not get pregnant. However, who can think of a safe way to stop this physiological necessity? No, right? It's never possible!

Terrible pregnancy! Terrible pregnancy!

— Juan Yin

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Eleven: Nighttime Talk of a Miserable Life, Originally a Dream; Scattered Footprints, the Wind and Rain are Too Oppressive.

Huanhua said: What are you laughing at? You all benefited from me. You know, I've been extremely poor these past few days. What else can I do if I don't find some money to use? It's raining today, and I'm not going back. I'll use this room for another day. The tea house attendant laughed: I didn't say anything, you're the one babbling on. Why bother asking for a room? Just move next door and save the money. Huanhua said: Don't talk nonsense. I'm staying here to be a matchmaker for Mr. Jia, and for no other reason. The tea house attendant said: Are you talking about that young lady who came from the west? It's already seven or eight tenths settled. What do you need to do as a matchmaker? Huanhua smiled: At the rate you guys are going, when would it succeed? One word from me, and you'll be drinking wedding wine right away. Before the two words "wedding wine" could be finished, someone outside was already chiming in: Wedding wine will definitely be drunk. As he spoke, the man had already walked in, repeatedly clasping his hands to him and saying: Congratulations, congratulations! Huanhua looked and saw that it was Li Shilian. He then laughed: What are you congratulating me for? A matchmaker is just running errands for others. Li Shilian laughed: Are you still pretending to be confused with me? I already received the tea house attendant's report a long time ago. At this time, the tea house attendant had already left. Huanhua blushed and said to him in a low voice: What did the tea house attendant report to you? Li Shilian laughed: He reported whatever you did. Huanhua was always afraid that he reported the matter of her stealing money. Therefore, she said: Did he say that I went to Mr. Jia's room? Li Shilian laughed: He didn't say you went, but that Mr. Jia came to your room. Huanhua didn't want to hide other things, so she laughed to Shilian: That's right, there was this matter. I'm still very grateful for your introduction last time. If it weren't for your introduction first, I still wouldn't know Mr. Jia by now. Li Shilian laughed: I know your purpose isn't his money. What conditions did you discuss with him? (174)

Qingdao Cherry Blossoms

— (Jin Junren)

Cherry blossoms are the national flower of the Three Islands (Japan). The Chinese people have never valued them much. The cherry blossoms of Qingdao are actually a legacy of its return (from Japanese occupation). In the fragrant March of spring, when the grass is lush and the willows are green, the flowers bloom all over the trees, dazzling like clouds of brocade. Looking closely, they are like a young girl's light rouge, her jade cheeks slightly flushed; looking from afar, they resemble ten thousand feet of silver silk, their brilliance dazzling. Today, the places with the most cherry blossoms are Zhongshan Park and the Japanese Shrine. The Japanese Shrine is a privately owned area of the Japanese, so the Chinese people rarely set foot there. Zhongshan Park is entirely a place for the Chinese people to visit and enjoy. When the flowers bloom in spring, tens of thousands of people crowd together. Various merchants also set up temporary stalls in the park to conduct business, which is what Qingdao calls the Cherry Blossom Festival. The festival period initially has no fixed rules, lasting about a week. After this, the flowers wither and the tourists are satisfied. In the park, there are Cherry Blossom Road and Double Cherry Blossom Road. On the former, a cherry tree is planted on each side of the road; on the latter, two trees are planted on each side. The cherry blossoms lining the road reflect each other like brocade. Walking beneath them, all worries disappear.

Records of Piao Miao Incense

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

When evening comes, after the sunlight has been collected, these silks, which have been dyed but not yet dried, must be brought indoors from the stone platform, to prevent the storm at night from ruining their colors. Inside the house, bamboo poles are not used, but a special wooden frame is used to hang them in twists and turns. These wooden frames are made very exquisitely, and are also painted with very beautiful colors. Sometimes, in good weather, the silk workers also directly carry these wooden frames out to dry the silk, which can save the trouble of taking them down from the frames and hanging them on bamboo poles again.

These silk-making girls do not need to wear court dresses or formal attire. They are free to wear all kinds of light and nimble clothing. Fortunately, they also have a lot of free time, which is perfect for spending on tailoring their own clothes. So, they dress up every day as if it were a holiday. And because there are many people and comparisons, they become extra motivated; if they were not afraid of being scolded by the Empress Dowager, they might dress even more prettily than prostitutes! (285)

Small Gardening

Clear Arrangement on the Desk

— Tian Sheweng

In the noisy city, having a small study with bright windows and a clean desk is truly a great happiness! With a small study, it should be neatly arranged. Although there is no need for a stand for books, a zither, or a peach mat, a quiet bamboo curtain rolled up and classic books laid out are essential. As for the arrangement on the desk, it should also be meticulous. It can both delight the eyes and expand the mind, please the emotions and gladden the heart; and it can also decorate and beautify, containing artistic meaning. Botanists say: "The branches and leaves of plants can release oxygen and absorb carbon." People's breathing releases carbon dioxide, which requires oxygen. Having plant displays on the desk, doesn't that absorb the carbon dioxide in the room and replenish oxygen? Cleaning the air and assisting breathing, plants have a close relationship with people.

For a clear arrangement on the desk, besides a miniature rockery and a few goldfish, potted flowers and bottle plants are the best. In this city of ten miles of marketplaces, there is not a single hill or valley to roam. In leisure, admiring the miniature rockery and carefully counting the fish, is that not the joy of climbing mountains and facing water? As for the potted flowers and bottle plants that are most suitable for the desk, there are several types:

(1) Narcissus. For a clear arrangement at the beginning of the year, red plum blossoms, heavenly bamboo, and narcissus are considered excellent, and these are displayed in the hall. Only the narcissus in a porcelain pot can be a clear arrangement on the desk. The goddess of the waves is extraordinarily graceful and charming. At this time, the red plum blossoms have already withered. It, along with orchids, in jade platters and golden cups, has a clear fragrance and is delicately enchanting. Is it not intoxicating? In botany, it is an annual herb with slender leaves and parallel veins, and a bulbous underground stem. Planted in a porcelain pot, protected with pebbles, and filled with clear water, it is even cleaner than lotus and orchids.

(2) Buddha's Hand Citron. Fragrant, the wax gourd are all displays for the desk; but the Buddha's hand citron is especially exquisite. The Encyclopedia of Flowers says: "The Buddha's hand citron tree is like vermilion music, with long, pointed leaves and thorns." In fact, it is an evergreen shrub, produced in Fujian, Guangdong, and other places, and is of the same species as the citron. The leaves are rounded, with thorns in the leaf axils, similar to orange, grapefruit, and mandarin orange plants. It blooms with five-petaled white flowers in the spring, and the fruit ripens in late summer, turning yellow and splitting at the top like human fingers, hence the name "Buddha's hand." Among plants, I like gourds and Buddha's hand citrons the most. Their postures are ingenious and exquisite, so moving. The Creator is truly inconceivable! The Buddha's hand has a refreshing fragrance. Without needing to pick flowers, it already forms hand seals. A clear companion on the desk, it is also enough to thoroughly understand the wonderful truth of the essence of reality.

(3) Rock Calamus. Calamus is a perennial herb that grows by the water. The ones with slender leaves are their variant, called "Rock Calamus." Planted in a tile pot, it is green and pleasing to the eye. Placed on the desk, it can not only be appreciated, but is also beneficial to health.

Page 17

Free Talk

The Use of Confucian Scholars

— Yang Changxi

Originally, Chinese literati have never given people a good impression. Of course, emperors of all dynasties have done some "using literature to convey the Way" when the world was at peace, but those engaged in literature only used literature as a stepping stone to advancement, as the saying goes, "excel in learning to become an official," and in reality only did a kind of idle play. It was either writing poems and composing odes for people to enjoy, or purely becoming a tool for praising virtues. It is truly said that reaching the "Confucian effect" mentioned in Xunzi's "Encouragement of Learning", is impossible to find many throughout the millennium.

Ancient literati were mostly called "Confucian scholars." The Duke of Zhou assisted King Cheng, "teaching and guiding King Cheng to understand the Way, and being able to conceal his achievements in the culture and military." And his behavior was called something that only a sage could do, so it was called "the great effect of a Confucian scholar." Other, relatively inferior Confucian scholars, "follow the former kings, promote ritual and righteousness, are cautious as subjects and bring honor to their superiors. If the ruler uses them, they will be in charge of the dynasty and be suitable. If they are not used, they will retire, educate the people, and must be obedient to their inferiors. Even if they are poor and hungry, they will not be greedy through evil means, and without a place to put an awl, they will be clear about upholding the great righteousness of the state." Others, Confucian scholars of a lower rank, are unworthy of mention.

Since Confucian scholars have the above-mentioned "Confucian effect," why are they scolded as useless things? This is naturally related to the social environment at the time, and their own impracticality is also a major reason. Regarding the social environment, the complaints expressed in the poems and essays of literati of all dynasties are enough to explain. Eight or nine tenths of their complaints ridicule and satirize things like "recognition." Just as Liu Xie said in the "Appreciation of Music" chapter of "The Literary Mind and the Carving of Dragons": "The appreciation of music is difficult! Music is truly difficult to understand, and to meet an appreciator is truly difficult to encounter. Is meeting an appreciator once in a thousand years?" Even if there is an appreciator, they only love novelty. For example: "When Chu said it first came out, and the Rhapsody on Shanglin Park was first composed, Emperor Qin and Emperor Wu regretted not being in the same era. Since they were in the same era, Han Xin was imprisoned and Ma Yuan was belittled..." This has already made literati sigh at the difficulty of recognition, and then added to the literary men's mutual contempt, similar to "envy among peers." In praising oneself and suppressing others, it is not only like Zhuang Zhou's laughter at the breaking of the Yang tree, and Song Yu's lament for white snow. Furthermore, their own "not valuing practicality, but only valuing empty words" inevitably led to setbacks everywhere. Even if one day their skills were sold, those who could "practice what they preach" and "work hard in a down-to-earth manner" were as rare as phoenix feathers and unicorn horns. Thus, Confucian scholars who talked about metaphysics and valued empty talk, compared to pragmatists (?), inevitably invited ridicule: "Literature adorned with hearts and broad belts, stealing the attire of the Duke of Zhou, bowing and shrinking; stealing the appearance of Confucius, their arguments and praises are stolen from Zichan and Zigong, their satire and criticisms on governance exceed the talents of Guan Zhong and Yan Ying, but their hearts are lowly, their ambitions small, and their positions limited; when given authority, they are confused and unable to govern..." (Huan Kuan's "Discourse on Salt and Iron," chapter on "Profit and Debate"). Even later Confucian scholars could criticize their measures from the responsibilities of officials, and even conceal their own valuing of empty talk by saying, "Without a position in the world, even Yao and Shun cannot govern the people," but the emptiness of their words and the sloppiness of their actions only led them to retreat and blame fate.

Although the mutual contempt among literati is "inherent since ancient times, and especially severe today," as Cao Pi said, I feel that Xunzi is the one who can stand in the position of a literati to criticize literati, and can instead point out the path for literati. In the chapter "Against the Twelve Philosophers," he strongly criticized those in the Warring States period who "adorned evil doctrines with false words to disrupt the world, with extravagant and deceptive words, making the world confused and unaware of the existence of right and wrong, order and chaos." There were Chen Zhong, Shi You, Mo Di, Song Xing, Shen Dao, Tian Pian, Hui Shi, Deng Xi, Wei Mou, Yi Bi, Zisi, Meng Ke, and twelve others. Zisi and Meng Ke were originally his predecessors, but he did not hesitate to criticize them, believing that Zisi and Meng Ke's sin was that they "neglected the laws of the former kings and did not know their system, and still their talents were great and their ambitions were large, their knowledge was mixed and broad; they examined the old ways and created the so-called Five Elements, which were extremely biased and irrelevant, obscure and without explanation, closed and without interpretation." Therefore, he decorated their words and respectfully said that they were the words of the former gentleman (Confucius). In Zisi's singing and Meng Ke's harmony, the world was deceived by them. In Xunzi's mind, he looked down on those Confucian scholars who could not summarize strategies, align words and actions, unify categories, and could not gather the heroes of the world and tell them of the great ancient teachings and teach them the ultimate obedience, and could not fully possess the articles of the sage kings and the sudden rise of the customs of a peaceful world within the audience hall and on the seat. The figures he idealizes are those who can "above, emulate the institutions of Shun and Yu, and below, emulate the righteousness of Zhongni and Zigong to seek peace." If this can be achieved, then there will be no gap for all those who strive to change the world with their own ways, and "the harm to the world will be eliminated, the affairs of benevolent people will be completed, and the traces of the sage kings will be manifested." But where are there truly such Confucian scholars in ancient and modern times?

In modern times, the morals of the world are declining, and corrupt Confucians are being eliminated day by day. The followers of the modernized Twelve Philosophers are everywhere. Everyone wants to take shortcuts to achieve fame and wealth. Who is willing to bury their heads in hard work to be a bookworm?

The Song of Zhaogao

— Gao Zhi

From Hefei to Chao County, the roadbed for the railway is being built. The roadbed occupies the people's fields. The landowners immediately get the land price, but the land tax must still be paid in full. The peasants cannot afford to submit a petition to sue, and there is no public opinion in the newspapers. So, someone said to a certain landlord, asking him to entrust a relative who is a member of the Supervisory Yuan to propose an impeachment case.

Zhaogao is a small place, but when commerce was prosperous, the British American Tobacco Company's cigarettes could sell up to two thousand cases a year. Each case paid a national tax of eighty yuan. So, a small place had to bear a national tax of 160,000 yuan a year on British American Tobacco Company's cigarettes. Other things can be imagined. However, in recent years, commerce has been sluggish, and the poverty of the countryside has become more acute. If the commercial index of 1928 is taken as 100, then the commercial index of Zhaogao in 1934 is only about 30. The vegetable oil lamp, which was driven into the poor countryside by kerosene, has come out again. Many families who light kerosene lamps are also using both kerosene and vegetable oil. The city and the countryside jointly express a high degree of poverty.

Those honest peasants have difficulty maintaining even a "hand-to-mouth" life. Some are burdened with rent, and some are burdened with debts. The creditors themselves are unable to maintain themselves, so they force the rent and force the repayment of debts. Those who can pay must pay, and those who cannot pay have no choice but to be taken to court. And those peasants who have neither the ability to repay nor the courage to struggle, and are limited by the dual oppression of hunger and debt, have no choice but to die, either by taking opium or by hanging themselves. Opium is as easy to buy as rice in the inland, and hanging oneself requires no expense.

Those who are slightly more lively, having never had the opportunity to be educated, of course do not know the root cause of poverty and the goals and methods of struggle, and are unwilling to starve to death. The only way is to take risks. Those who stand on the heads of the peasants, eating their fill and growing fat, talk about benevolence and morality in spring chairs. The so-called "cunning" peasants who cannot even live comfortably in thatched huts have no choice but to become bandits on the yellow earth road, robbing their fellow villagers. Often at dusk, people carrying dozens of copper coins are also robbed.

They are truly without food to fill their hunger. Even the "New Year's Eve dinner" that is valued by the general public is impossible for many poor people to prepare. If they don't become bandits, they will starve to death. So, around the Lunar New Year, the hometown is plagued by bandits. Although "unlawful" bandits were executed on New Year's Eve, robberies still occurred. And large groups of bandits are brewing an act of robbing a town at the junction of Hefei and Chao County. So, the local area is panicking day by day. News of small market towns being robbed is often heard. The two counties send troops to suppress them, but the bandits cannot be completely eliminated, at least not before the fear of hunger is resolved. Many villages cannot find three silver dollars, nor can they find three dou of white rice. They eat yellow turnips, wild vegetables, buckwheat, sweet potatoes, corn, and the like. It is expected that people will starve to death between the second and third months of the lunar calendar.

Many rural families leave their hometowns and go to the cities to seek a living, especially women. And those who cannot even wait for employment or are trapped in desperation have no choice but to sell their daughters to others as servants, and selling girls to others as maids is the most common. Ordinary girls can be sold very easily for thirty or forty yuan. Although the law states that men and women are equal and prohibits the trafficking of people, due to poverty and hunger, the trafficking of people in the inland is as common as the open sale of "black rice" in "earthen shops." Even in Nanjing, I have seen refugees shouting and selling their children on Zhongshan Road and heard of the fact of selling girls.

Another emergency solution is to engage in prostitution. It is common for poor women in cities to engage in prostitution. This wind of prostitution, however, along with foreign goods and syphilis, has blown into the countryside. Rural women go to cities and towns to engage in prostitution for money. The price is only one or two yuan each time, and sometimes even only twenty or thirty copper coins. Although it is so little in the eyes of people in the city, it is considerable in the eyes of rural, impoverished, and ignorant women. So, venereal diseases are transmitted from the cities to the towns and then from the towns to the countryside. There are no modern hospitals in the countryside, and the germs spread wider and wider, resulting in the "deepening into the people" of opium and syphilis and truly "working hard at the grassroots level." Sedan chair carriers also smoke opium, and innocent peasants also contract venereal diseases.

In just over ten days, I reviewed the lives of the lower classes in the inland. The trafficking of people and other pitiful events caused my brain, which had been numb for two years, to have a slightly tired reaction. Although there is something I want to say, I don't have the enthusiasm to say it like before.

On the Motive of Writing

— Bai Lai

"I don't care at all whether I have genius, or whether what I write is good or bad. I am simply telling myself. And that is all I need. Why? Because, in my opinion, writing is not serving something else, it is merely a means of developing oneself." Artzybashev once confessed in this way. This kind of motivation for writing solely for "developing oneself" has existed since ancient times. The reason it appears more blatant and vulgar today is simply that the scope of individual life has been limited by an unreasonable social system to the point where it can no longer be reduced. "Writing" has become a means for those who value themselves above all else to strive for a lifeline of their own.

Naturally, no one is a sage who can forget themselves. Moreover, many sages, as Voltaire said, are just big liars. Therefore, even if Balzac only poured his sincerity into every work, and his purpose was merely to write in order to "pay off debts," he was still a great author. The problem here is that as an author, in order to achieve goals other than writing, he would not hesitate to violate the truth, thus becoming a poisonous weed, which is truly sickening. I now have some understanding: why an author once shouted out the cry, "I want to break away from the ranks of literary people." Precisely because as a literary person, one loves to protect "oneself" the most. Furthermore, it is well known that our literary world has buried the efforts of many young literary talents. However, we these latecomers in writing, often overvalue our own efforts, and thus curse, complain about, or even insult our predecessors; this is equally unworthy of emulation.

Understanding this point, then it can be expected that "enlightened" authors will no longer write for their own vanity, status, fame, and fortune. Because of the socialization of the production system, people will break through "self" and write for "society." Moreover, only such authors are worthy of building an immortal monument in the hearts of millions of readers.

Vegetable Vendor Liang Hu Zi

— Wu Guanglue

It was already past noon.

Vegetable vendor Liang Hu Zi still had a full load of vegetables on his shoulders. When he set off from home in the morning, this load of vegetables weighed heavily on his shoulders, and now it was still this load of vegetables; how futile it was for time to pass by second by second, and for the fatigue of trudging from this village to that village! Liang Hu Zi, feeling the coldness and despair of business, could not help but shed tears, and sobbed softly at the sadness of his own fate.

He was already fifty-one years old this year, with sparse and gray hair, sunken eyes, a black and soft long beard, high cheekbones, and missing teeth... In short, everything about him was a sign of approaching old age. At his age, if he had been born into a rich family, he would definitely be eating idle meals all day, accompanying his grandchildren and enjoying the happiness of his later years. But how disrespectful the Creator was to him! Now, for the sake of his old wife and his own two meals a day, he had to work hard and run around! "Life" was such a serious and cruel matter for him!

"Anyone want to buy green vegetables?"

He wandered around the ends of the alleys, shouting in a hoarse voice. His trembling tone echoed in the silent space, all the more implying a kind of miserable feeling. In such a year of famine and disaster, all the villagers felt the extreme difficulty of life, and even the necessities of "food" were almost impossible to afford, so how could they have extra money to buy vegetables? Even though Liang Hu Zi raised his voice and shouted with all his might, it was all in vain.

"The world has changed!"

He sighed again in a hoarse voice. He recalled the past: at that time, he would carry a full basket of vegetables out in the morning, and sell them all after touring three or two villages. He remembered the scene when the villagers rushed to buy when the vegetable load stopped; he remembered the pleasure of leisurely going to the teahouse alone when the green vegetables were sold out: remembering all this, a wave of smiles flashed on his lips again. But now, he had run through five villages, large and small, and the vegetables were still so full in the load! Struck by this cruel event, he couldn't help but sigh again in a sad and hoarse voice.

Despairingly, he ran towards another village again. He anxiously looked at the sun, and then at the vegetables in the basket: he was silently considering the fate of his goods. The glittering rays of the sun shone on his thin face covered with sweat, that face was like a clay statue in a rainstorm, making people feel pity and fear. His bright eyes stared at the dull sky, silently proclaiming like a devout Christian praying:

"God, it would be good if the years changed..."

He walked on the desolate and winding village road. The surroundings were deathly silent. In this human world as miserable as a funeral vault, in addition to bearing the heavy burden of the vegetable load on his shoulders, all beautiful and foolish dreams floated in his mind. Like such an ignorant old man, apart from resigning himself to fate, what else did he know that someone could change everything?

Mr. Ju Qing (7)

— Ke Ling

Being a school board member naturally required someone with status and prestige in the town. For example, the famous gentleman Zhang Xiaofeng had such qualifications. Before this term, he had served as a school board member of the district elementary school for five consecutive years, with his younger brother Xiaoyan in charge of everything, serving as the principal. For the first three years, for some reason, Mr. Xiaoyan was suddenly elected as a member of the county party headquarters thanks to the promotion of a classmate; then Zhang Xiaofeng was also honorably appointed as the preparatory director of the district office in this town, and the two brothers both rose rapidly in their careers. Once they let go, the school board member of the district elementary school was replaced, and the president of the town's Chamber of Commerce, Chu Runfu, took over the position.

Originally, everyone was a figure in the community, and their personal friendships were excellent, so "enthusiasm for education" could naturally be shared without distinction. However, since last summer, when Zhang Xiaofeng's son, Youxiong, graduated from the county middle school and returned, after being idle at home for half a year, the situation changed a little.

It is said that the results of the district elementary school have not been good in the past two years, so at the beginning of spring, someone launched a re-election of the school board members, and as a result, Zhang Xiaofeng returned to the position.

Then young master Youxiong took office and took over the position of principal.

However, things don't seem to be that simple. On the one hand, the school has already started, and when collecting funds from all parties, they all said that the former school board member had taken them away; the former school board member's finances, the seal, and important documents have not been handed over. After several negotiations, there was no result, so a storm was brewing.
