Shen Bao This Port Supplement

Talks

What Kind of Books Should Young People Read

— Meng Ruo

What is shown in the restoration movement is naturally the ancient air. Like the recent large and small bookstores, they are reprinting ancient books such as Siku Quanshu, Tu Shu Ji Cheng, and the Twenty-Five Histories, and Twenty-Six Histories. This is also a phenomenon of restoration.

In present-day China, there are indeed many people who like to tumble in the piles of ancient books. Those who are poisoned by ancient books are not counted; most of them take pride in considering themselves ancient people. A group of sages of the time, for the sake of their own status, have to pretend to be antiquarians, and decorate their bookshelves with a few ancient books to show their enthusiasm for promoting the restoration movement. There are also those who strongly advocate and promote reading ancient books, and those who are forced to read ancient books. Therefore, ancient books are reprinted in response to the situation!

However, since some people in the current intellectual class like to read ancient books, there is naturally a need to reprint ancient books. On the other hand, since some people like to read new books, there is naturally a need to compile and select new books. These are all digressions.

The question is here: At present, in the Chinese publishing industry, ancient books are being reprinted, and new books are also being compiled and selected. As a modern Chinese youth, should we read ancient books and study a little ancient knowledge? Or should we read new books and absorb some new knowledge? If this question is not entirely meaningless, then it is necessary to bring it up for discussion.

In our view, modern Chinese youth should read new books and should not read ancient books. The reasons are as follows:

First, knowledge is constantly changing. Therefore, we are constantly pursuing new knowledge, and where do we have the leisure to browse ancient books?

Second, knowledge is a tool for life. Modern people should live a modern life, so modern Chinese youth should also acquire some new knowledge in order to adapt to the living environment.

Third, the culture of a country can only survive by moving forward; retreating will lead to destruction. Modern Chinese youth have the mission of promoting the forward development of Chinese culture. Therefore, our task is to create a new culture.

Fourth, even if ancient books are treasures, we can only obtain various knowledge that meets the needs of the times from new books.

Therefore, when the trend of reprinting ancient books is prevalent today, we can still have this Chinese New Literature Series to read, which can be said to be the good fortune of modern Chinese youth!

Home

— Qin Jian

"The green grass of March is like oil, our family takes a foreign ship to drift away: the spring tide rolls thousands of miles away, the girl at the field head is sad in every way." Singing, the noisy singing voice floated leisurely on the river again: these simple, popular sentences, paired with a series of stiff local accents, even if they were unpleasant, were more than enough to make the old boatman yearn. A kind of nostalgia for the homeland rose uncontrollably like a thick fog, following this intimate and familiar local accent, the mountains and rivers of the homeland appeared in fantasy and memory, the faces of the relatives and friends of the old homeland appeared, and the rouge-colored lovely traces of the youthful age in the homeland also appeared - the youthful page was still very clear in front of him, but the era had already turned a cruel, green face without mercy, and people trembled in front of it wearing the mourning clothes of old age, the good days were, finally like the waves that passed under the boat, like the early spring tide, one pushing another, forever, without looking back, rushing towards the endless front, and then dissipating.

At the age of over fifty, he still carried the innate nature of loving the sea and loving the water, and lonely rowed a small boat: whether it was a gentle breeze or a violent storm, he always refused to rest for a day and floated on the river, waiting for the shouts of the guests on the shore: "Hey, boatman, crossing the river, crossing the river!" So, while responding with a cadence, he gratefully and eagerly pulled the boat close, let the guests board the boat, and then pulled the boat to the other side, the guests crossed the river, and when they went ashore, they left ten or five copper coins, and gathered the copper coins every day, buying rice, measuring oil, and perhaps going to the street to buy a zhang of blue cloth on festivals, if there were a few extra copper coins, he would accumulate the extra ones into silver corners, and then accumulate the silver corners into a big ocean coin, and hide them in the cloth bag under the cabin board. So, the serpent-like years passed easily page by page, blurred almost like reeds.

(He is also a person with parents, wife, and children, but his hometown is like a firecracker behind a string of days: fighting, fighting back and forth, on a day many years ago, a battalion of soldiers came to the village, and then in less than a month, they started firing, two old ones, one ate a bullet, one died of illness, and the young wife who had only been married for less than a year was also dragged from under the bed by five soldiers one night, still carrying a five-month-old fetus in her belly, and...

Home has been destroyed in a fire, his own son fled for thirty miles on a muddy road at night, and pretended to be dead in the pile of corpses, and that's how he managed to escape with his life after three days and nights, wandering like a beggar. A year and a half later, the war was over, and he returned home: the house was gone, the woman and his parents were gone, and only a dilapidated small ferry boat was left in the swamp.

Lowering his head, the tide in the river rose in April, and the boat drifted like autumn leaves, so: wiping his wet eyes, dragging the broken boat out.)

From then on, he forgot about home, forgot about the world, but learned the old sailor's wandering tune: "Ai ya ai, drifting through five lakes and four seas; spring tide, spring tide, you go, a man leaves home and never looks back!"

The spring tide does not know how to flow back, and a man's drifting does not know how to go home. In this way, fifty years have passed by glittering with the silver light in the spring tide once a year, the old boatman has no home, the old boatman's hometown is the water country rippling with the spring tide.

The boat, in the end, also seemed dilapidated in a lifetime of drifting, and what about people? ... No, when the wind in the third month of spring blows again, facing the surging river water, the old boatman also sighed, also remembered something, lingering, with endless depth and distance.

Suddenly a shout of "Hey"! - Someone on the shore called for a crossing.

Days of Worry

— Ding Xing

The hoe digs down, but the heart is not in the digging.

Many things were spinning around in my heart, spinning so much that my head ached, and after thinking about it, I couldn't figure anything out.

—The Xue family's two loads of rent are already from the year before, can they get through the end of this year? Let's plan this first.

—But Li Tu Zi's twenty yuan with three-point interest, paying interest every month can't hold up! Damn it! Borrowing twenty yuan from him, the interest paid is enough for the principal for several months!

—Those small debts on the street are not a small amount either, unless you don't want to walk on the street, how can you get rid of these?…

—That evil creature, born of a prostitute! Dare to say I'm poor! Even if my old man is so poor that he's begging for food, shouldn't a wife scold me for "not being promising?" Really a heartless prostitute!

Furiously, the hoe dug down, but the heart was not in the digging: "Bang!" With a sound, the hoe hit a rock, and sparks splashed in all directions; waking up suddenly, he picked up the hoe and took a look, "Damn it! A big gap!" He spat and cursed.

The work stopped like this, and he took a few steps forward and sat down on a bluestone. The sun was shining on his head, warming him, there was no wind, there was, just a little - it was a warm winter afternoon blowing a southerly wind.

Veins were bulging on his forehead, and A Da seemed to be dreaming: he recalled the full warehouse of sweet potato rice left to him by his father when he died three years ago, and a few sections of bright sweet potatoes - ah, those bright sweet potatoes! Where have they all gone now? Wasn't it all spent on courting that dead demon? And now, now that he is poor, even she has become like this!

—Is there really such a thing in the world? The thunder won't strike her to death! Finally, he stood up fiercely again, grabbed the hoe like a bandit, and dug down hard, "Bang" Another stone! A stone? He lowered his head, yes, it was indeed the same stone as before!

—Damn it! Is even a stone looking for trouble with me? Fine! Let's say I'm possessed by a ghost today, I'm going back to his mother's house!

So he carried the hoe on his back and walked slowly along the winding field bank towards the village; his heart seemed to be hanging in another world, and the gentle breeze caressed his flushed face, but he didn't feel it at all.

—Hey! A Da! Send those few rice accounts over the day after tomorrow, okay?

It was the owner of the rice store at the entrance of the village shouting across the counter. He was startled and raised his head sharply, and realized that he had already entered the village, so he stopped, looked at the owner of the rice store, and immediately replied:

—Yes! I know, don't keep urging me every day!

When he saw the two half-closed doors of his house in the distance, the scene of the morning quarrel immediately intensified and disturbed his mind, and his troubles made him not want to go home: but

Page 20

a pair of disobedient feet finally moved him to the front of the door.

In order to show some prestige to the people inside, he raised his foot and kicked the door in heavily, he thought: If this works, she will come out to see me immediately, then everything will be fine!

However, it was quiet inside, not only did no one come out, but there wasn't even a "Who is it?" He cursed in his heart and stepped into the door, unloaded the hoe, and threw it casually towards the corner of the door, rushing into the room angrily.

The room was dark, and he couldn't see anything when he first entered the room. He held his breath and paused for a while, then fixed his eyes and looked at the bed: there was no one there at all, the bed was empty.

A premonition quickly broke into his consciousness, his heart jumped, and he quickly turned his head: the only box he had next to him was open and empty, like it had been robbed, facing him!

—Ah, it's over! Anger immediately sank from his body, and his eyes were dizzy. He fell straight down onto the bed...

A shout of "Is A Da at home?" came from outside.

Spring Rain

— Lin Feng

It is also a heavy sky,

It is also drizzling rain,

It is also a hazy lake;

You say: The heavy sky is the time of wind and rain,

The drizzling rain is the tears of parting,

There are arc sails on the hazy lake surface rushing on their way.

That was a few years ago, when we were about to part, we were all saying goodbye on this lake; at that time, everyone had the heart of a young man, wanting to do something for people's careers, wanting to be firm, wanting to be brave, wanting to be earth-shattering: in the drizzling rain, we each rushed on our own way; among us, some people regarded the hazy lake surface as a kind of evil force, the mental strength of young people made young people want to open a path in the haze, even if only a lone sail was left, they still had to row forward, even if the lake surface was hazy again, the haze would definitely let young people open a path. We all thought this way, in the drizzling rain and hazy lake surface, we said goodbye.

However, that goodbye, some actually became farewells with me forever.

It is also this time, it is also this sky, this rain, this lake surface: and facing this scene, there is only me alone. Thinking of so many friends, how many people have died before their ideals: "Work hard," their words are still in my ears: thinking back to my own life in recent years, walking to the old place where they once set foot, it made me silently stare at the lake surface, for a long time, I was just silent. The lake surface in front of me is still hazy, how many hazes have I rushed through? Does the water surface still have some water ripples of my own progress? Thinking, I am just silent!

I know very well that many friends have rushed to that side, even if the result has never been effective, they died; but that is still admirable; compared to those who live in vain, how much stronger is it? In silence, I also felt some anger; "Work hard" their words, I will never forget.

Anger is still difficult to suppress the past. No matter what, I think of that young man with disheveled hair, from entering prison to dying, when I tread on the place he once trod, in anger, I cannot help but feel sad. The emotions of young people are so precious, so endearing. It will ignite another part of the heart fire of young people, they are all young people, they love each other, understand each other, it is so easy, so sincere, so deep.

What shall I say to this hazy lake surface? I am still only silent. The willows sprout tender buds again, the peach blossoms bloom silently, and wither silently. Nature always repeats like this, taking away some in the repetition, and bringing some back. It's always like this; how can it allow you not to go? Yes, "Work hard," the spring rain brings me this message. Commemorating the friends who died for their ideals, I will never forget their words.

It is also a heavy sky,

It is also drizzling rain,

It is also a hazy lake;

I say: The heavy sky is the time of wind and rain,

The hazy lake surface does not see the shadow of your lone sail,

The drizzling rain, is just drizzling rain.

Yes, the rain beats the peach blossoms, and also beats the tombs in the wilderness, the dead are dead, and what about the living?

Could it be that the drizzling rain is tears?

"Lost"

— Qingquan Made

One Year Old

— Sakura no

The child is exactly one year old! The night before, my wife whispered softly in my ear as we were about to sleep.

Sunday, when the dawn breaks, it will be such a refreshing climate! A gentle breeze kisses my cheeks, bringing a soft and comfortable feeling.

Turning my head, my son lay in the inner bed, his bright, round eyes fixed on me! Then he gave me the cutest wink, pursing his lips!

(He seems to feel delighted at being one year old!)

I woke my wife up, and she asked what to buy for the child as a gift. I pondered in my mind, slowly getting dressed.

With a heart full of anticipation, I walked out of the house. I calculated whether the value in my pocket matched the goods I wanted to buy.

In a shop, I saw a very lovely little children's suit, priced at two dollars and seventy-five cents. The shop assistant enthusiastically wrapped it up in colored wrapping paper. I had to reach for the wallet in my pocket without further delay.

As I turned around, I saw a very polite little sailor hat, also giving me a warm salute, as if very eager for me to take it home with me.

It seemed like the easiest kind of temptation to sway one's original intentions! When returning home, I still had it tucked under my arm.

My wife quickly put the clothes on the child. The child pulled hard on the brim of the hat, refusing to let go. My wife then happily said to herself:

"Doing it this way, Dad is very thoughtful."

In the afternoon, my wife suggested taking a photo of the child as a memento! It also occurred to me that today was my son's birthday. In a letter my mother sent a week ago, she wrote very earnestly that we should buy a pair of incense sticks and candles to pray to the Bodhisattva on that day. So I asked if we needed to buy these things.

I knew this was still her most familiar mischievous way of asking indirectly, and I used my mother's tone to agree to this matter.

She said we should buy some cheaper dishes today! I finally couldn't help but smile at her.

Before and after the meal, she didn't mention taking photos or anything like that again.

"It's our son's birthday today, don't you dare hit him or scold him carelessly."

While washing the dishes, I don't know how she remembered this, and she said it to me as if reminding me.

"Let's take our son to get a photo taken!" I said to her frankly.

"How did you remember again?" she said, but then looked at me carefully a few times, as if suspecting that these words were not sincere.

I smiled at her. I picked up the child in my arms, and she smiled happily too.

After taking the photo at Guanghua Studio, my wife looked particularly happy. Let's take a stroll back!

We quickly paced a long way back and forth on Avenue Joffre, my wife leaning on my shoulder.

Let's pray that our son will always be adorable.

Classical Chinese Prose

Wang Yongmei's Donglai Bo Yi

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Yu Fu Assassinating Duke Yin (Continued)

Duke Yin's integrity in abdicating the throne was very clear in his heart and obvious in his actions. When Duke Huan was young and weak, if Duke Yin had other ambitions, even a slight hint would have been nipped in the bud. Duke Huan was in Duke Yin's control for eleven years. Not only was there no conflict, but he was also nurtured and raised. There is heaven above and earth below, and his heart and actions cannot be fabricated. The only regrettable thing is that his righteousness was not complete, that he coveted power for a few years and did not abdicate quickly. Because he did not abdicate quickly, the appearance of reluctance was shown outwardly. Yu Fu was thus able to carry out his plot to assassinate Duke Huan. If Duke Yin had retired bravely with a noble spirit, intimidating people, then the unrighteous would not dare approach his wall, and the unjust would not dare approach his courtyard. How could they dare to plot an assassination and sully my hand with treacherous deeds? Now Yu Fu dares to openly express his rebellious words without fear, which must be because Duke Yin showed signs of reluctance, inviting this. Duke Yin still did not take warning, and even told Ruofu, "It is because he is young. I will give it to him. Make preparations for the [mourning] clothes. I am getting old."

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

A Brief History of Film Development (X)(II)(Continued from March 8th)

— Wen Ying

(XII) Forerunners of Sound Film Invention

"A Brief History of Film Development," previously published in this journal, totals eleven sections, and due to the intermittent nature of the original text, it is also divided into three parts for sequential publication. The first part, consisting of five sections, was published from January 7th to 11th; the second part, consisting of six sections, was published from March 3rd to 8th; and this is the third part, which is also the last part. This is specially noted for the convenience of readers.

The history of film development is like a person struggling through hardship and adversity, experiencing many years of failures and successes, until reaching a position of wealth and honor. However, after reaching that position, they begin to feel that the sun declines at midday and the moon wanes after being full. But after thirty years of struggle, has film, which has changed from "moving magic lantern shows" to a great enterprise, also begun to decline after reaching its peak? From the perspective of machinery, finance, and personnel, film had reached its zenith at that time. However, after reaching its zenith, the film industry began to decline. The number of viewers in cinemas was dwindling. Film industry giants felt that the end of film had arrived.

Someone said at that time, "What we need is a good revolution. The entire film industry needs to be reformed. Otherwise, it will be difficult to save the fate of the film industry." Many people laughed at his words, not understanding what he was saying. Perhaps even the speaker did not know what he was saying, because he was simply guessing and expecting. But they did not know that at that time, several dedicated people were working hard in secret rooms. What were they doing? No, they were trying out a new invention, preparing to start a revolutionary storm in the film world. These few people decided to make the films that had been coming and going for a decade or two talk and sing!

This is the birth of sound film! When sound film was born, the great inventor Edison had not yet died. The ability of films to speak was originally something Edison had dreamed of. Now that dream had suddenly come true, it is unknown what Edison thought when he first saw a sound film. But in fact, Edison did not think that the film itself would produce sound. What he imagined was simply connecting the phonograph and the film projector, so that one could hear the sound from the phonograph while watching the film.

We have seen this kind of "sleeping in the same bed, dreaming different dreams" sound film in the early days of sound film. Their dialogues or songs were recorded on records, and when the film was being played, the dialogues and songs on the records were broadcast using a wireless sound amplifier. The biggest drawback of this invention was that it was very complex, very bulky, and it was difficult to synchronize the actions on the screen with the sounds on the record, and there were often discrepancies. Later invented sound films had synchronized action and sound, because the sound was emitted from the film itself. But that was later.

Before the invention of modern sound films, William Fox and his chief engineer Theodor EU Chase first publicly demonstrated his "sound structure" attached to the film. That kind of sound structure was similar to the sound structure on records, but the former was attached to the film, while the latter was wound on the record. At the same time, Warner Brothers also invented a structure that connected films and records. But when the film industry giants heard the results of their inventions, they all shook their heads and said, "This kind of thing is not advanced enough, and cannot be shown to the audience!"

How high had the audience's standards risen! They did not want to see things with rough and uneven sound. But thirty years ago, they had all watched the first moving picture, "The Great Train Robbery," and expressed amazement. When that kind of film was being screened, the vertical lines of light flickered above and below, like rain in the room. When a group of actors performed, they jumped up and down like a group of monkeys. But they all liked to watch that kind of film, and thirty years later, in 1926, when they saw the rough sound films, they refused to even look at them. This shows how surprisingly fast the audience's standards have risen. (To be continued)

Review of "Anne of Green Gables"

— You Jing

——Showing at the Great Shanghai

Anne of Green Gables

After watching "Anne of Green Gables," it feels like reading a clear and sorrowful little poem by a small stream in the refreshing autumn air, facing the white duckweed and red smartweed.

From the perspective of the artistic conception of this "Anne of Green Gables," the worldview of the original author, L.M. Montgomery, is undoubtedly quite outdated. He writes:

When the orphan Anne was fourteen years old, she was taken in by a brother (Matthew), who decided not to marry because of a broken heart in his youth, and a sister (Marilla), who accompanied him in remaining single into old age. She lived with these two old people, whose lives were unhealthy and whose nature was somewhat perverted, which was not very suitable for her, although she was orphaned, but extremely lively nature. Because she had red hair, she was given the nickname "Carrot" by her male classmates. She violated school rules, and the strict old maid, upon hearing that the other party, Gilbert, was the son of her brother's heartbroken lover, did not punish her, but when Anne loved this young man, Gilbert, she was subjected to extremely severe interference, and even forced to break off contact with him. As a result, the unmarried old adoptive father became seriously ill, and Anne managed to get a famous doctor from Gilbert to save him, and these two old people allowed their engagement.

Here, the original author wants to express the theme that the love of the next generation should not lose its freedom due to the misfortune of the love of the previous generation. However, he did not seek to develop this from the next generation, Anne and Gilbert, actively fighting for their own right to love freely, but passively wanted the old people to feel grateful for the saving of the sick before they would allow it. This point of view explains the author's worldview.

The film "Anne of Green Gables," due to the original work's abundance of natural poetic charm, and the ethical and emotional background; as well as the director George Nicholls Jr.'s delicate and concise approach, has achieved considerable results. But it is not without its shortcomings in terms of the script, apart from the outdated worldview mentioned above. First of all, the Marilla family originally wanted to adopt a boy from the orphanage, but unexpectedly adopted Anne, a girl, by mistake. As for why the mistake happened, and why it was not corrected at the time, the film does not explain it clearly. Secondly, the next day, when Marilla decided to send Anne back to exchange her for a boy, how could the head of the orphanage have taken her to send Anne to the Cuff family to be a maid, and made Marilla take her back again because she couldn't bear to see Anne suffer? This not only shows that Marilla's psychological change of love and pity for Anne is too fast, but also that it is unreasonable for her to go to the Cuff's. Thirdly, although Anne ignored Gilbert because he teased her, causing her to violate school rules, when she learned of the relationship between Gilbert's family and the Marilla's, she already had a great curiosity about him, and Gilbert repeatedly expressed his remorse and admiration to her. Under these circumstances, it was very possible for her and him to make up. However, the film must follow the same old pattern as the love process commonly seen in other films, making Gilbert save her life in danger before earning her grateful love. This is not only a cliché, but also a great show of artificiality.

The director's success lies first in the fact that the emotional components are grasped strongly. Everywhere is full of laughter, but this laughter is enough to make people cry. Secondly, the sound effects are handled well. There are many places in the film that use the strengths of silent films, such as when Anne offended Mrs. Cuff at the Cuff's house and was about to be driven away, and when Matthew came to find a way to keep her, etc., all using silent scenes and heavy lines to achieve valuable results. As for the use of light and shadow, such as Anne's lonely double shadow, old Matthew's slender and charming shadow, and the background when Anne repents to Mrs. Cuff, are all excellent comparisons to the chaotic light during classmates' outings and the flower shadows in Green Gable.

In terms of acting, in addition to Anna Shirley, who had good results in "Little Women," gaining further progress here, Old Matthew, played by O.P. Heggle, is the most successful. Gilbert's early performance is too suggestive of a bad seed. Although he is a bit naughty, he shouldn't give people a bad impression, so that people can sympathize with him when he is later forced to lose his freedom.

Dickens' Class Consciousness in "David Copperfield"

— Fo Lei

Charles Dickens, one of the three major novelists of the first half of the nineteenth century, is, like many novelists such as Zola, Stevenson, and Galsworthy, now valued by Hollywood film producers. This naturally shows that Hollywood film producers are running out of film subjects and have to look for subjects from existing famous literary works and adapt many literary classics into films.

Thus, Dickens' "A Tale of Two Cities" and "Oliver Twist" have been produced before, and now "David Copperfield" is being shown in Shanghai.

It is impossible to evaluate Dickens' literary career and works in this limited space. I just want to talk briefly about "David Copperfield," which may be helpful for film viewers to refer to.

Through the protagonist in "David Copperfield," from his childhood to his adulthood, Dickens not only created such a lovely and struggling character for us, but also realistically wrote about the middle class and the poor at that time, their lives and moral concepts. In this "David Copperfield," David's friend Micawber is often an optimist troubled by economic difficulties and creditors, almost a microcosm of his father, who was also forced into prison by debt, while his mother sold furniture to maintain her life. In addition, many of the characters are almost what he encountered in his childhood. In this novel, the only character who can be called upper class is Steerforth, but how does the author describe him? He seduced Ham's fiancée, later abandoned her, and finally drowned at sea. Here, Dickens does not harbor any goodwill towards the upper class: although there is no more intense attack, the satire is sharp enough.

The entire story of "David Copperfield" is extremely simple and touching, full of warmth and friendship. Old Peggotty, his search for Emily, and Ham jumping into the sea to save his rival, these descriptions are very emotional.

With George Cukor, who succeeded in directing "Little Women," to control this story, which is also full of emotion, there is considerable confidence in the results. Actors such as Washa Wen, Leon Barrimua, and Olive are all familiar and beloved characters to movie fans, and their acting skills will undoubtedly be able to develop perfectly under the guidance of such an experienced director.

In "David Copperfield," the scene where David is in his mother's arms, the actor playing the young David is child star Freddy Bartholomew and Elizabeth Allen—showing at Nanjing

Three Women in a Storm

Fan Xuepeng's personality was the strongest. She used her "great hands" to work. Chen Yan was a lonely girl. Unable to leap through the dark society, she attempted suicide by drowning but was rescued. Lu Lixia was a romantic female student, a believer in optimism, singing "Sunny Day" and "Beautiful Youth" every day, but in the end, she still suffered deep stimulation.

Movie Novel

Amateur Reporter (After Office Hours) (1)

— Tong Yun

Produced by MGM, starring Clark Gable and Constance Bennett.

A large car, moving silently, stopped in front of the New York News Recorder newspaper building. The chauffeur, fully uniformed, immediately jumped out and went to open the car door. As soon as the door opened, a graceful woman emerged. That was Sharonna Scott. Her slender figure stood by the sidewalk, the wind blowing her clothes, truly giving a fairy-like impression. She looked at the platinum diamond-encrusted watch on her wrist and said, "Come at half-past six," and walked into the tall newspaper building.

Inside the newspaper building, on a glass door were written the four characters "Chief Editor." Inside was a large desk. The person sitting at the desk was combing his hair with his fingers. He was very young, with dark, slightly curly hair. Although young, he was extremely familiar with the ins and outs of the news industry and knew everything. Because he knew so much, he inevitably became impatient with those who were less knowledgeable.

Now, this chief editor, Jim Brown, was talking to a photographer. That photographer, Barr, considered himself to be a top-notch photographer in the field. Jim held several photos in his hand, examining them with a frown for a long time, and asked him what they were. Barr excitedly told him that those were all the photos from the Peterson case. He said that he had spent three whole days and nights to take them.

The Peterson case, indeed, was now the talk of the town. A wealthy man, a beautiful wife, and a handsome man supplying the object of pursuit for a wealthy wife. But what are these? Rumors, or facts? Jim said to Barr, "What's the story?" Barr was taken aback and said, "Story? How would I know those things?" Jim shook his head and said, "The entire island of New York is gossiping about the Peterson case, him and his wife... and that Pennister, can't our big newspaper find out some real news? Then what do we want these photos for? To put them in frames and hang them up? We must find a way! No matter how difficult! I don't know how to find it, but I know it can be found!"

As he spoke, he slammed his fist on the table. Suddenly, he saw a news draft on the pile of papers, with only the two letters "N.S." Jim picked it up and looked at it. It turned out to be a music review, but after reading three lines, he already felt it was out of place and terrible. He couldn't help but wonder, "Hey... who wrote this? Who is N.S.?" Barr said, "She is a socialite. She's only been here for a month. The general manager's wife recommended her." Jim said, "Hey, a socialite? Call her in, I want to see her."

Barr answered and backed out. He closed the door as he left. When the door opened again, the graceful woman who had just stepped out of the car had already slowly walked in front of Jim. Jim couldn't help but feel his heart pounding. He had never seen a woman dressed like this in his life. Her quiet demeanor made a seasoned chief editor uneasy. But he still deliberately pretended to be rude and asked, "Who are you?" The other party calmly said, "You asked me to come. Didn't you want to see me?" She smiled slightly as she spoke. Jim then nodded and said, "Oh, so you are N.S." (To be continued)
